Somewhere around 21:32 or so, the watch said "CalWatch has unfortunately stopped." But why?
Clearly, for the past few hours beforehand, things were not going very well, with all these START
messages from the ActivityManager. By the time I checked the time at 21:32, it was clearly
time for things to go kaboom. CalWatch started right back up again without missing a beat, but we
would obviously prefer for users not to see that.

Later on, I tried to collect a debug trace, but this logcat shows that, by then, everything
I cared about was long gone.

The most telling lines are these:
11-21 21:32:31.260 V/MyViewAnim(26290): starting new draw thread
11-21 21:32:31.260 V/ActivityManager( 1752): Display changed displayId=0
11-21 21:32:31.280 F/Looper  (26290): Could not create wake pipe.  errno=24
11-21 21:32:31.280 F/libc    (26290): Fatal signal 6 (SIGABRT) at 0x66b2 (code=-6), thread 3617 (Thread-1097)

So... CalWatch is resuming the draw thread and, whatever a wake pipe is, we blew chunks on it.

Not helpful:
http://stackoverflow.com/questions/17606111/a-looper-could-not-create-wake-pipe-errno-24

Suggestive but not exactly on point:
http://stackoverflow.com/questions/15203271/could-not-create-epoll-instance-errno-24
http://yongbingchen.github.io/blog/2013/03/11/resource-leakage-in-android-java-apk/

The errno=24 line is generated in Looper.cpp when it tries to call pipe(), the low-level Unix
system call and seems to indicate that there were too many files already open. So... somehow, we're
keeping files live for too long.

In other contexts, we've seen evidence of running out of file descriptors. Fixing this is going
to be tricky. For now, we'll just have to remember this for later. Hmm.
